*NOTE*  For the majority of the time I worked for Mr. Fish, I relied
on Microsoft Hotmail for email services.  I have saved every email I
was able to once I realized that they would be important.  Most of my
outgoing emails were not saved because the default option was to only
save sent mail if a checkbox was clicked which I usually didn't think
to do.  Hotmail has a 2MB limit on mailbox size && I have had 1MB of
mine occupied by email between Mr. Fish && myself since this all
happened.  He used to regularly send me enormous attachments which
I've had to delete along with the messages they were attached to due
to the above space limitations.  I have salvaged every email that I
was able to.
  When it became apparent that I would need to print them out, I had
to forward them all to another email account so that I could download
them in a text format.  Whenever I had to resend an email I originally
sent, I included a -> (To?) line whenever it wasn't being sent solely
to Mr. Fish.  I also included the date originally sent when possible.
I wish I could just provide access to my email account since all this
hard copying obscures the natural progression of correspondence and
is therefore somewhat difficult to follow.  The read messages are all
bunched together && the sent messages follow so chronological order
may be difficult to determine just by the flow of responses.
  At least this document contains a time-stamped record of issues,
arguments, && emotions.  Hopefully I can just refer to particularly
relevant sections as pointed evidence of Mr. Fish's constant
irrational accusations, arguments, unreasonable new requirements, etc.
  So in summary, I'm sorry that this record is not more complete but
it's the best I could do under the circumstances and I will work with
it to the best of my ability.  Hopefully it contains plenty to clearly
demonstrate that I was never malicious with Mr. Fish && worked as
diligently as I could until I needed to acquire additional income to
afford my living expenses.

-Philip Stuart
p.s. Since I write code predominantly in a programming language called
"Perl", I often intentionally misspell werds into or out of Perl-like
spellings to reflect how technical or how much I liked doing something.
Thus, if I enjoyed doing some coding, I usually called it "werk".
Similarly, if I describe a person who not be technical or fun to deal
with (in my opinion), then I might refer to them as a "jirk".  This is
just a playful mechanism I have made up to subtly categorize several
common things that I deal with regularly (eg. the werld, lerning,
serfing, etc.).  I also occassionally misspell words that rhyme with
"ink" to be "inq" since I registered a domain for my server that is
an acronym pronounced "BinK" but spelled "BinQ".  Common examples of
this are "thinq" && "linq".

Content-Type: text/plain; format=flowed




>From: "Len Fish" <leonard3@home.com>
>To: "PIP TIGGER(2)" <piptigger@hotmail.com>
>Subject: Simple secure permissions and  Passwords input method
>Date: Fri, 12 May 2000 19:52:21 -0700
>
>PIP
>
>Here is a simple way to implement the permissions administartive function. 
>While it requires an employee ID or Vendor ID if the user is not a 
>customer, it is a high security page.
>
>Therefore while it would be convenient to insert the permissions in the 
>employee or vendor tables, it is not practical because of the lower level 
>permissions that those pages will have assigned.
>
>I think tables like the demo ones you set up, not unlike an Excel 
>spreadsheet would serve as an adequate input screen. There could be one for 
>permissions and a different one for employee salaries.
>
>The key column in the spreadsheet- like table would be employee or vendor 
>#, and the next field would be Username, then password, then hint. The next 
>column would be basic security level for read, then basic security level 
>for write, (numbers1-20) date of change (auto insert), followed by 15 
>columns for exceptions. The exception columns would name the table and/or 
>field followed by 2 alpha characters. Y for enable or N for restrict, 
>followed by R for read only, W for write only, or B for both read and 
>write. The exception colums would override the basic permission level only 
>for the tables and fields named.
>
>I think this is a clean input method for our administrators, while not 
>requiring  a tricky input page layout.
>
>Len

>Pip:
>
>You should take a look at etoys.com. It is at least 60% Open Merchant.
>
>They also have integrated a co. called babycenter.com, which overall is a 
>better site. They fill the screen with their pages nicely.
>
>BabyCenter uses a more conventional sku as you may note.
>
>Anyway, I suppose we are stuck for the time being at least with OM's SKU.
>The fourth character they call a store code. It is useless as that. Even in 
>etoys it is always zero. Funny as it is supposed to be alpha. Maybe its an 
>OH.
>
>I think we can live with the OM system, but we will make the 4th character 
>a part of the last 3 digits so we can have more than 999 selections within 
>the first 3 alpha characters.
>
>Thus sofq103 would be manufacturer or service etc., sof and the discrete 
>item would be Q103.
>
>We can also assign a meaning to the fourth character for quick visual and 
>computer sorting, like C is for a clearance item, and A is for an auction 
>item.
>
>Actually their concept of only 3 numerics at the end could get us in 
>trouble someday. I'd love to see 6 digits reserved with a fill of trailing 
>zero's till we need the number. The program could ignore all trailing zeros 
>in case someone leaves them out, or puts in the wrong number of zeros. We 
>would never actually end an sku with a zero.
>
>I believe Open Merchant left the "store code" so that you could have a 
>"mall" with many stores in it. Not something we care about. Besides our SKU 
>  table tells us everything we need to know about the sku, including what 
>"store" it could be found in, if we ever needed it.
>
>Take a quick look at etoys.com, it has a great number of good ideas, but 
>needs to be spread out on the screen.
>
>Also a quick look at BabyCenter.com.
>
>Len

>Pip-
>
>Sometime when you get the chance, not necessarily this week, the following 
>refinement program should be written for the password module if you have 
>not done so already.
>
>Legally, if anyone in the company knows an employee's password, even the 
>root administrator, you cannot hold an employee legally responsible based 
>on anything they may have done identified by the password they operated 
>under.
>
>Thus we should generate a randon PIN at the time they come on board and 
>give it to them. There should be an admin page (not graphic designed, just 
>plain vanilla) where any employee can change their pin number as long as 
>they know the old one. They will be instructed to immediately change that 
>pin given to them and change it in the future any time they believe their 
>pin may have been compromised.
>
>The pin should be stored encrypted, and shown as asteriskd when they type 
>it in (twice for comparison). I don't think we should use the hint thing 
>for employees. People are too litigious.
>
>Throughout the system, if someone, anyone,  inserts their pin number 
>incorrectly four times in a one hour period, lock the account and print out 
>the fact in an exception file which automatically is generated for 
>management once every 24 hrs. If suddenlt there are more than x lockouts in 
>a 10 minute the period, the system administrator must be notified at once, 
>plus the person on duty for the current shift.
>
>Give me a call Sunday, when you are awake.
>
>Len
>
>Len

>if ($FORM{'SHIPSTATUS_inp'}=3D'sp') {

>}  else {
>      $shipst=3D'backordered';

>
>open(MAIL,"|$mailprog -t");
>print MAIL "To: $site->{'order_email_address'}\n";
>print MAIL "From: $site->{'customer_service_email_address'}\n";
>print MAIL "Bcc: $FORM{'UID'}\n";
>print MAIL "Subject: $title\n\n";
>print MAIL "Your order is being $shipst \n";
>print MAIL "Date: $FORM{'SDATE_inp'}\n";
>print MAIL "Shipper: $FORM{'SHIPPER_inp'}\n";
>print MAIL "Comments: $FORM{'COMMENTS_inp'}\n";
>print MAIL "Order ID: $FORM{'orderid'}\n";
>close (MAIL);
>
>

>values ('$lineid', 'lineid', 'SDATE', '$FORM{'SDATE_inp'}') ";
>          $q2=3D"insert into extraprop (objid, objkind, fieldname, body) =

> > Hey Len,
> > I just wanted to give you an update on my progress.  After the 
>preliminary
> > testing on Tue. and a stronger one yesterday afternoon, it became 
>apparent
> > that security concerns (in regards to database access) hadn't been
> > sufficiently addressed.  I thought of ways to circumvent the security
> > measures originally developed.  I researched and read for almost 2 hours
> > last night about CGI security methods and special procedures for state
> > retention.  I originally had the permissions residing within the same
> > database as the rest of the data (these permissions determine who can
>access
> > anything whatsoever from databases to users to actual data records to
> > files).  Last night I designed two solutions and after much 
>consideration,
>I
> > decided on one and began coding it (to be more secure this time around).
> > That's what I'm working on right now.  Previously, with some creative 
>html
> > submission, users could override their own permission level and with 
>that
> > access, simply set their permissions higher which would enable 
>everything
>to
> > be compromised.  The new design basically segregates each level 
>according
>to
> > how damaging a security breach could be.  This means that basically only
>the
> > super user can access the database and user permission tables.  I've 
>also
> > had to add a new criterion for testing which enables partial creations.
> > This has taken a lot of time since all the code tests need to reflect 
>this
> > new field too and it's not behaving properly just yet.  This new 
>structure
> > should prove much more reliable and secure.  I'm planning to get this 
>all
> > done by tonight (hopefully bugs fixed too).  I've also done some server
> > maintenance while you were gone which removed the openmerchant virtual
>host
> > and other settings which were involved with the development version of
>that.
> >   I've left most of the files on the server (in case we can benefit from
> > their code or data structures etc.) but I've removed them from the 
>apache
> > configuration and cleaned up the web server operation methods.  I've 
>also
> > looked at Dynamic.net this week to see if we could setup
> > len@800telephone.com (& pip@800 etc.)through them and it seems that all 
>of
> > their email packages cost money and aren't included with most of the
>hosting
> > options.  If you were emailed special instructions on what services are
> > included with our hosting package or how to specifically setup email
> > aliases, please forward them to me so I can make more progress on that

> > services directly from the 800tele server but I didn't get a chance to

>
>Len
>
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store
>Sleepycat Software offers Berkeley DB in configurations targeted at 
>different applications. The Transactional Data Store product is our 
>high-end database offering. Richer in features than both Berkeley DB Data 
>Store and Berkeley DB Concurrent Data Store, Berkeley DB Transactional Data 
>Store provides the power and flexibility of high-end database management in 
>a compact, easy-to-use package.
>
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store is intended for programmers writing 
>applications that need a fast, scalable transactional data store with 
>support for disaster recovery. It permits multiple users to read and write 
>data in the database at the same time, and uses a fine-grained locking 
>scheme to maximize concurrency and minimize contention for data. It 
>includes a logging service that permits multiple changes to the database to 
>be grouped into transactions, and to be committed or rolled back 
>atomically. The log and data files can reside on separate disks, so that 
>databases can survive catastrophic loss of either disk. Berkeley DB 
>Transactional Data Store's features, performance, and reliability are 
>unmatched in the embedded database market.
>
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store uses the same on-disk storage 
>structures, or access methods, as our other database products. It provides 
>an easy-to-use C API for storing, searching for, and updating records. 
>Other APIs are available separately.
>
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store provides enterprise-class data 
>management services to programmers without the complexity, size, and 
>management headaches of the relational products available from other 
>vendors.
>
>Features
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store offers the following features:
>
>   a.. Full source code availability.
>   b.. Small footprint (as small as 150Kbytes).
>   c.. Easy-to-use C API.
>   d.. Uses native O/S file system for storage.
>   e.. Thread-safe implementation.
>   f.. Database dump and load utilities.
>   g.. Support for keys and values of arbitrary data types, including 
>programming language data structures.
>   h.. Keyed and sequential traversal for retrieval, insertion, 
>modification and deletion.
>   i.. Retrieval into user-specified or allocated memory.
>   j.. Partial-record data storage and retrieval.
>   k.. Cursors.
>   l.. Joins.
>   m.. Memory-mapped read-only databases.
>   n.. Architecture independent databases.
>   o.. Individual databases up to 248 bytes.
>   p.. Key and data values of up to 232 bytes.
>   q.. Single- or multi-user read-write database access.
>   r.. Fine-grained, high-concurrency locking strategy permits readers and 
>writers to share access to a single database, and minimizes contention for 
>data.
>   s.. Before and after-image logging.
>   t.. Database recovery after application or system failure, including 
>catastrophic failures.
>   u.. Online ("hot") database backups.
>   v.. General-purpose lock, log, transaction and shared memory buffer pool 
>with standalone interfaces.
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store is Sleepycat's enterprise-class 
>embedded multi-user database engine. It provides the reliability, 
>protection, and performance of much more expensive products in an 
>easy-to-use package targeted precisely at professional software developers.
>
>Scalability
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store maintains caches and other shared data 
>in shared memory. As a result, threads of control in the same process, or 
>in other processes, can share data pages read from disk. Data read by one 
>process is available to others. This improves performance for virtually all 
>database applications.
>
>All of the Berkeley DB products have been carefully designed to support 
>large databases and high concurrency. Berkeley DB can address up to 256 
>terabytes of data in a single database. Sleepycat Software customers have 
>single databases that are hundreds of gigabytes in size in daily use. 
>Berkeley DB is able to support thousands of threads working on a single 
>database at a time.
>
>Growth Path
>Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store is our high-end data repository. 
>Applications with less stringent demands can use Berkeley DB Data Store or 
>Berkeley DB Concurrent Data Store. As the demands on those applications 
>increase, they can step up to Berkeley DB Transactional Data Store easily. 
>All three products use the same underlying data file formats, and the APIs 
>that they support are compatible up the product line. 2 2
>

>"Thanks for your note.
>
>It turns out that you were right and I was wrong -- in the
>haze of the trade show floor, I mistakenly told you there
>was a DBI interface to Berkeley DB.  There's not.  However,
>there are some alternatives I want to let you know about.
>
>First, the latest MySQL release (3.23.18, from www.mysql.com)
>already includes Berkeley DB.  When you create a table, you
>can choose to use the original MySQL ISAM (myisam), and the
>table will behave as in previous versions of MySQL -- no
>transactions, no failure recovery.  Alternatively, you can
>choose to use Berkeley DB as the storage engine (bdb), and
>you will get transaction-protected updates and full recoverability.
>
>Of course, there is good DBI support for MySQL, so this may
>give you what you need.
>
>Second, you can use the BerkeleyDB package to interface to
>Berkeley DB from Perl.  The package was developed by Paul
>Marquess at BT, and supports all the transactional interfaces
>in Berkeley DB.  It's available from CPAN.
>
>Sorry for the confusion."
>
>mike

>AN excerpt from below "<-->Linux Notes
>-----------
>
>Newer versions of Linux (e.g. RedHat 6) ship with a C library that has
>a version of Berkeley DB linked into it. This makes it very difficult to
>build DB_File with anything other than the version of Berkeley DB that
>shipped with your Linux release. If you do try to use a different
>version of Berkeley DB you will probably get the error described in the
>"Incompatible versions of db.h and libdb" section of this file.
>
>As yet I haven't found a satisfactory way around this problem. If you
>do know a workaround to this problem which doesn't involve replacing
>the built in version of Berkeley DB I would like to hear from you."pip
>
>
>
>BerkeleyDB Version 0.11 4th Jun 2000 Copyright (c) 1997-2000 Paul Marquess. 
>All rights reserved. This program is free software; you can redistribute it 
>and/or modify it under the same terms as Perl itself. DESCRIPTION 
>----------- BerkeleyDB is a module which allows Perl programs to make use 
>of the facilities provided by Berkeley DB version 2 or 3. (Note: if you 
>want to use version 1 of Berkeley DB with Perl you need the DB_File 
>module). Berkeley DB is a C library which provides a consistent interface 
>to a number of database formats. BerkeleyDB provides an interface to all 
>four of the database types (hash, btree, queue and recno) currently 
>supported by Berkeley DB. For further details see the documentation in the 
>file BerkeleyDB.pod. PREREQUISITES ------------- Before you can build 
>BerkeleyDB you need to have the following installed on your system: * Perl 
>5.004_04 or greater. * Berkeley DB Version 2.6.4 or greater The official 
>web site for Berkeley DB is http://www.sleepycat.com The latest version of 
>Berkeley DB is always available there. It is recommended that you use the 
>most recent version available at the Sleepycat site. The one exception to 
>this advice is where you want to use BerkeleyDB to access database files 
>created by a third-party application, like Sendmail. In these cases you 
>must build BerkeleyDB with a compatible version of Berkeley DB. BUILDING 
>THE MODULE ------------------- Assuming you have met all the prerequisites, 
>building the module should be relatively straightforward. Step 1 : If you 
>are running either Solaris 2.5 or HP-UX 10 read either the Solaris Notes or 
>HP-UX Notes sections below. If you are running Linux please read the Linux 
>Notes section before proceeding. Step 2 : Edit the file config.in to suit 
>you local installation. Instructions are given in the file. Step 3 : Build 
>and test the module using using this sequence of commands: perl Makefile.PL 
>make make test INSTALLATION ------------ make install TROUBLESHOOTING 
>=============== Here are some of the problems that people encounter when 
>building BerkeleyDB. Missing db.h or libdb.a ----------------------- If you 
>get an error like this: cc -c -I./libraries/ -Dbool=char -DHAS_BOOL 
>-I/usr/local/include -O2 -DVERSION=\"0.07\" -DXS_VERSION=\"0.07\" -fpic 
>-I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503/i586-linux/CORE BerkeleyDB.c 
>BerkeleyDB.xs:52: db.h: No such file or directory or this: cc -c 
>-I./libraries/2.7.5 -Dbool=char -DHAS_BOOL -I/usr/local/include -O2 
>-DVERSION=\"0.07\" -DXS_VERSION=\"0.07\" -fpic 
>-I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503/i586-linux/CORE BerkeleyDB.c 
>LD_RUN_PATH="/lib" cc -o blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so -shared 
>-L/usr/local/lib BerkeleyDB.o 
>-L/home/paul/perl/ext/BerkDB/BerkeleyDB/libraries -ldb ld: cannot open 
>-ldb: No such file or directory This symptom can imply: 1. You don't have 
>Berkeley DB installed on your system at all. Solution: get & install 
>Berkeley DB. 2. You do have Berkeley DB installed, but it isn't in a 
>standard place. Solution: Edit config.in and set the LIB and INCLUDE 
>variables to point to the directories where libdb.a and db.h are installed. 
>Wrong db.h ---------- If you get an error like this when building this 
>module: cc -c -I./libraries/ -Dbool=char -DHAS_BOOL -I/usr/local/include 
>-O2 -DVERSION=\"0.07\" -DXS_VERSION=\"0.07\" -fpic 
>-I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503/i586-linux/CORE BerkeleyDB.c 
>BerkeleyDB.xs:93: parse error before `DB_INFO' BerkeleyDB.xs:93: warning: 
>no semicolon at end of struct or union BerkeleyDB.xs:94: warning: data 
>definition has no type or storage class BerkeleyDB.xs:95: parse error 
>before `0x80000000' BerkeleyDB.xs:110: parse error before `}' 
>BerkeleyDB.xs:110: warning: data definition has no type or storage class 
>BerkeleyDB.xs:117: parse error before `DB_ENV' ... This error usually 
>happens when if you only have Berkeley DB version 1 on your system or you 
>have both version 1 and version 2 (or 3) of Berkeley DB installed on your 
>system. When building BerkeleyDB it attempts attempts to use the db.h for 
>Berkeley DB version 1. This perl module can only be built with Berkeley DB 
>version 2 or 3. This symptom can imply: 1. You don't have Berkeley DB 
>version 2 or 3 installed on your system at all. Solution: get & install 
>Berkeley DB. 2. You do have Berkeley DB 2 or 3 installed, but it isn't in a 
>standard place. Solution: Edit config.in and set the LIB and INCLUDE 
>variables to point to the directories where libdb.a and db.h are installed. 
>Undefined Symbol: txn_stat -------------------------- BerkeleyDB seems to 
>have built correctly, but you get an error like this when you run the test 
>harness: $ make test PERL_DL_NONLAZY=1 
>/home/paul/perl/install/bin/perl5.00503 -Iblib/arch -Iblib/lib 
>-I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503/i586-linux -I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503 -e 
>'use Test::Harness qw(&runtests $verbose); $verbose=0; runtests @ARGV;' 
>t/*.t t/btree.............Can't load 
>'blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so' for module BerkeleyDB: 
>blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so: undefined symbol: txn_stat at 
>/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503/i586-linux/DynaLoader.pm line 169. ... This 
>error usually happens when you have both version 1 and version 2 (or 3) of 
>Berkeley DB installed on your system and BerkeleyDB attempts to build using 
>the db.h for Berkeley DB version 2/3 and the version 1 library. 
>Unfortunately the two versions aren't compatible with each other. 
>BerkeleyDB can only be built with Berkeley DB version 2 or 3. Solution: 
>Setting the LIB & INCLUDE variables in config.in to point to the correct 
>directories can sometimes be enough to fix this problem. If that doesn't 
>work the easiest way to fix the problem is to either delete or temporarily 
>rename the copies of db.h and libdb.a that you don't want BerkeleyDB to 
>use. Undefined Symbol: db_appinit ---------------------------- BerkeleyDB 
>seems to have built correctly, but you get an error like this when you run 
>the test harness: $ make test PERL_DL_NONLAZY=1 
>/home/paul/perl/install/bin/perl5.00561 -Iblib/arch -Iblib/lib 
>-I/home/paul/perl/install/5.005_61/lib/5.00561/i586-linux 
>-I/home/paul/perl/install/5.005_61/lib/5.00561 -e 'use Test::Harness 
>qw(&runtests $verbose); $verbose=0; runtests @ARGV;' t/*.t 
>t/btree.............Can't load 'blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so' 
>for module BerkeleyDB: blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so: undefined 
>symbol: db_appinit at 
>/home/paul/perl/install/5.005_61/lib/5.00561/i586-linux/DynaLoader.pm ... 
>This error usually happens when you have both version 2 and version 3 of 
>Berkeley DB installed on your system and BerkeleyDB attempts to build using 
>the db.h for Berkeley DB version 2 and the version 3 library. Unfortunately 
>the two versions aren't compatible with each other. Solution: Setting the 
>LIB & INCLUDE variables in config.in to point to the correct directories 
>can sometimes be enough to fix this problem. If that doesn't work the 
>easiest way to fix the problem is to either delete or temporarily rename 
>the copies of db.h and libdb.a that you don't want BerkeleyDB to use. 
>Undefined Symbol: db_create --------------------------- BerkeleyDB seems to 
>have built correctly, but you get an error like this when you run the test 
>harness: $ make test PERL_DL_NONLAZY=1 
>/home/paul/perl/install/bin/perl5.00561 -Iblib/arch -Iblib/lib 
>-I/home/paul/perl/install/5.005_61/lib/5.00561/i586-linux 
>-I/home/paul/perl/install/5.005_61/lib/5.00561 -e 'use Test::Harness 
>qw(&runtests $verbose); $verbose=0; runtests @ARGV;' t/*.t 
>t/btree.............Can't load 'blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so' 
>for module BerkeleyDB: blib/arch/auto/BerkeleyDB/BerkeleyDB.so: undefined 
>symbol: db_create at 
>/home/paul/perl/install/5.005_61/lib/5.00561/i586-linux/DynaLoader.pm ... 
>This error usually happens when you have both version 2 and version 3 of 
>Berkeley DB installed on your system and BerkeleyDB attempts to build using 
>the db.h for Berkeley DB version 3 and the version 2 library. Unfortunately 
>the two versions aren't compatible with each other. Solution: Setting the 
>LIB & INCLUDE variables in config.in to point to the correct directories 
>can sometimes be enough to fix this problem. If that doesn't work the 
>easiest way to fix the problem is to either delete or temporarily rename 
>the copies of db.h and libdb.a that you don't want BerkeleyDB to use. 
>Incompatible versions of db.h and libdb 
>--------------------------------------- BerkeleyDB seems to have built 
>correctly, but you get an error like this when you run the test harness: $ 
>make test PERL_DL_NONLAZY=1 /home/paul/perl/install/bin/perl5.00503 
>-Iblib/arch -Iblib/lib -I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503/i586-linux 
>-I/usr/local/lib/perl5/5.00503 -e 'use Test::Harness qw(&runtests 
>$verbose); $verbose=0; runtests @ARGV;' t/*.t t/btree............. 
>BerkeleyDB needs compatible versions of libdb & db.h you have db.h version 
>2.6.4 and libdb version 2.7.5 BEGIN failed--compilation aborted at 
>t/btree.t line 25. dubious Test returned status 255 (wstat 65280, 0xff00) 
>... Another variation on the theme of having two versions of Berkeley DB on 
>your system. Solution: Setting the LIB & INCLUDE variables in config.in to 
>point to the correct directories can sometimes be enough to fix this 
>problem. If that doesn't work the easiest way to fix the problem is to 
>either delete or temporarily rename the copies of db.h and libdb.a that you 
>don't want BerkeleyDB to use. If you are running Linux, please read the 
>Linux Notes section below. Linux Notes ----------- Newer versions of Linux 
>(e.g. RedHat 6) ship with a C library that has a version of Berkeley DB 
>linked into it. This makes it very difficult to build DB_File with anything 
>other than the version of Berkeley DB that shipped with your Linux release. 
>If you do try to use a different version of Berkeley DB you will probably 
>get the error described in the "Incompatible versions of db.h and libdb" 
>section of this file. As yet I haven't found a satisfactory way around this 
>problem. If you do know a workaround to this problem which doesn't involve 
>replacing the built in version of Berkeley DB I would like to hear from 
>you. Solaris Notes ------------- If you are running Solaris 2.5, and you 
>get this error when you run the BerkeleyDB test harness: libc internal 
>error: _rmutex_unlock: rmutex not held. you probably need to install a Sun 
>patch. It has been reported that Sun patch 103187-25 (or later revisions) 
>fixes this problem. To find out if you have the patch installed, the 
>command "showrev -p" will display the patches that are currently installed 
>on your system. HP-UX Notes ----------- Some people running HP-UX 10 have 
>reported getting an error like this when building this module with the 
>native HP-UX compiler. ld: (Warning) At least one PA 2.0 object file 
>(BerkeleyDB.o) was detected. The linked output may not run on a PA 1.x 
>system. ld: Invalid loader fixup for symbol "$000000A5". If this is the 
>case for you, Berkeley DB needs to be recompiled with the +z or +Z option 
>and the resulting library placed in a .sl file. The following steps should 
>do the trick: 1: Configure the Berkeley DB distribution with the +z or +Z C 
>compiler flag: env "CFLAGS=+z" ../dist/configure ... 2: Edit the Berkeley 
>DB Makefile and change: "libdb= libdb.a" to "libdb= libdb.sl". 3: Build and 
>install the Berkeley DB distribution as usual. FEEDBACK -------- How to 
>report a problem with BerkeleyDB. To help me help you, I need of the 
>following information: 1. The version of Perl and the operating system name 
>and version you are running. The complete output from running "perl -V" 
>will tell me all I need to know. If your perl does not understand the "-V" 
>option is is too old. BerkeleyDB needs Perl version 5.004_04 or better. 2. 
>The version of BerkeleyDB you have. If you have successfully installed 
>BerkeleyDB, this one-liner will tell you: perl -MBerkeleyDB -e 'print 
>"BerkeleyDB ver $BerkeleyDB::VERSION\n"' If you haven't installed 
>BerkeleyDB then search BerkeleyDB.pm for a line like this: $VERSION = 
>"1.20" ; 3. The version of Berkeley DB you have installed. If you have 
>successfully installed BerkeleyDB, this one-liner will tell you: perl 
>-MBerkeleyDB -e 'print BerkeleyDB::DB_VERSION_STRING."\n"' If you haven't 
>installed BerkeleyDB then search db.h for a line like this: #define 
>DB_VERSION_STRING 4. If you are having problems building BerkeleyDB, send 
>me a complete log of what happened. 5. Now the difficult one. If you think 
>you have found a bug in BerkeleyDB and you want me to fix it, you will 
>*greatly* enhance the chances of me being able to track it down by sending 
>me a small self-contained Perl script that illustrates the problem you are 
>encountering. Include a summary of what you think the problem is and a log 
>of what happens when you run the script, in case I can't reproduce your 
>problem on my system. If possible, don't have the script dependent on an 
>existing 20Meg database. If the script you send me can create the database 
>itself then that is preferred. I realise that in some cases this is easier 
>said than done, so if you can only reproduce the problem in your existing 
>script, then you can post me that if you want. Just don't expect me to find 
>your problem in a hurry, or at all. :-) CHANGES ------- See the Changes 
>file. Paul Marquess

>
> > I have read this carefully and I have mixed feelings about it.  Stable
> > builds of opensource software end in an even sub-version number if they
>are
> > reliable and an odd one if they are developmental/unstable/implementing
>beta
> > features etc.  This means that Perl version 5.6 is a stable release that
> > they want normal people to use as it has passed all the regression 
>testing
> > and meets all their stability requirements to be used widely.  Perl 5.7 
>on
> > the other hand should only be used by Perl developers who are werking
> > towards Perl 5.8 since it has not likely passed all the tests and is the
> > ground to experiment with potential new implementations or features.  
>Perl
> > 5.7 might crash everytime you do something simple (depending on what
> > developmental features were compiled into the particular build you got).
> > The version of MySQL that we are currently using is the most recent 
>stable
> > version that I saw when I downloaded it (version 3.22.32).  Any MySQL
>driver
> > that is in the under-development (3.23.xx) tree may not be stable or
> > reliable.  Since we are in a development phase of 800Tele, I wouldn't
>worry
> > too much if the database server crashed once in a while but if the
> > BerkeleyDB component never makes it into a stable release build of MySQL
> > (like the upcoming 3.24), I might be worried about employing a database
> > suite that is known to not have been held to the same standards as 
>release
> > versions.  We may develop on 3.23.xx and find it to be perfectly stable
>and
> > then it might not be a concern.  My recommendation is to stick with
>database
> > engines that are most likely to be very stable.  With that in mind, 
>would
> > you like me to install this development version of MySQL (3.23.18) so 
>that
> > we can see how difficult it will be to enable our code to benefit from 
>the
> > transactional features mentioned by Mike?  TTFN & Shalom.

>STATISTICS REQUIREMENTS
>
>July 2, 2000
>
>Pip:
>
>Here are the Statistics. Doing these should help develop some modular, math 
>functions for manipulating the data base, that can be re used with web page 
>calls. These stats are designed to allow marketing and operations people to 
>tune the site and merchandising for optimum results.
>
>All items marked beow with an asterisk are to accumulated for real time 
>display (a few minutes delay is ok if needed to to keep the system from 
>degrading, i.e. low priority) between midnight East Coast time, and 
>11:59:59 P.M. the same day. I.E. 24 hours. A chron program stores the daily 
>totals for archival use by the date once the day ends.
>
>BTW for both of our further knowledge; E.G. is for the Latin Exempli Gratis 
>and means for example. I.E. is from the Latin Id Est, and means That is. 
>I'll try to stick to that convention in the future.
>
>* Number of unique users (from distinct urls.) For the month to date.
>
>As a batch job, the number of above since inception of the site
>
>* Grand total of hits thus far today
>
>* Number of page views total thus far today
>
>* Average number of page views per login
>
>* Average length of time on a page
>
>* Ranking of pages visited most (products included) sorted by top ten
>
>* Number of logins who failed to put in E-mail address
>
>* Number of logins who failed to purchase anything
>
>* Number of logins who used our help button
>
>* last page viewed before logging off (or being disconnected) sorted by top 
>10.
>
>* Top 10 products ordered
>
>* First time users today
>
>* Log of total logins totaled by hour i.e. (24 numbers)
>
>Ping times to New York and Florida once every 10 minutes
>
>* If possible longest disk request delay during the 24 hour period
>
>* Highest percent usage of ram by hour
>
>Power fails by time , hour, minute and date
>
>System resets by time, hour, minute and date
>
>* number of people locked out by hour for trying incorrectly for 3 times by 
>hour and date
>
>* number of old users who returned to use site sorted by times they have 
>returned. Part of that may be a night batch job
>
>* Total Dollar amount of sales in real time
>
>* Average dollar amount per order
>
>* Average length of total login by user
>
>* Average dollar order sorted by amount and length of total time on site 
>both with and without using help button.
>
>Any questions or comments are welcome , of course.
>
>Len

>From: "Len Fish" <leonard3@home.com>
>To: "PIP TIGGER(2)" <piptigger@hotmail.com>
>Subject: comments on description
>Date: Tue, 4 Jul 2000 12:55:58 -0700
>
>Here is a marked up summary so you can update your text.
>
>Still no e-mails from the Bot.
>
>Len
>
>PIP
>
>I have tried to clean up your very nice discription. Look for the ***. 
>Often Ideleted words immediately befre or after the *** without mentioning 
>it, so read the new sentence for clarity.
>
>
>
>This file was created by Pip Stuart on June 28th, 2000 for the purpose
>
>of describing the software functionality developed thus far for
>
>800Telephone.
>
>The system is primarily composed of 3 programs:
>
>index.cgi - The default script which validates passwords and handles
>
>all secure administration processing.
>
>dp.cgi - This script is a slimmed version of index.cgi which
>
>specializes in DynamicPages only. It lets index.cgi
>
>validate the login and takes the handoff from there.
>
>pw.pl - This is utility employed by the above scripts to
>
>handle an abstracted method for generating and
>
>processing unique session identification codes.
>
>Almost everything in the system (from users to protected pages to data
>
>fields to images) has 3 different permissions associated with it. They
>
>are: Read, Insert, and Delete. The system validation checks each
>
>permission level according to the requested operation. Lower permission 
>numbers apply to users with higher security levels. E.G. a user with 
>permissions Read=0, Insert=0, & Delete=0 has no restrictions on what he is 
>able to do in the system. He would be allowed to do anything in an area of 
>the data warehouse or basic code for which he has a valid password number.
>
>As permissions ascend, the limitations on available options increase. For 
>now, a user
>
>with Read=256, Insert=256, & Delete=256 is the most restricted 
>user****(such as a )
>
>named customer. Priviledged users can specify the levels which limit
>
>the use of each operation. This means that an administrator (or
>
>superuser with premissions 0,0,0) could grant full access to all users
>
>or specify any number of arbitrary groups to partition users according
>
>to permission levels and accessible options. It will be meaningful for
>
>the remainder of this document to describe all operations from the
>
>perspective of a system administrator to detail each included function
>
>and feature. Every user with ***(more restrictive) permission levels will 
>have
>
>diminished access according to the administrator's designation.
>
>For a user to be able to read a protected page (or view a particular
>
>dynamic image), the user must have a Read permission level that is less
>
>than or equal to the Read ***(permission) level associated with the page 
>(or image).
>
>For a user to be able to overwrite ***(data or code or an image on) a 
>protected page, the user must have an Insert permission level and a Delete 
>permission level that are both
>
>less than or equal to the ***(security) levels associated with the page.
>
>***(paragraph)
>
>For a user to be able to delete a protected page (or graphic file), the
>
>user must have a Delete permission level less than or equal to that of
>
>the page (or image). Individual database element modifications have the
>
>same 888(secure) properties.
>
>***(For eample l)et's assume that there exists an account in the system for 
>a user named
>
>"superman" with a password of "souper" who has the highest permissions
>
>(0,0,0). Superman can point his browser to the login script (currently
>
>http://24.16.72.254/demo/index.cgi) and specify "superman" and "souper"
>
>as his Username and Password respectively in order to login to the
>
>system. If an incorrect password was supplied, an error message is
>
>returned and the account name (in this case "superman") is written to a
>
>logfile containing failed login attempts with timestamps. If any user
>
>supplies 3 errant passwords within a single hour, their account is
>
>automatically locked for a 24 hour period.
>
>Each account has an associated hint field. If a user has forgotten their 
>password, ***(but knows their account name) they can check the box 
>***(trailing --remove the word trailing) "Show hint?" and the Login will 
>return with their hint (this (does) not count as a failed login attempt(. 
>Remove the word either)
>
>After "superman" has logged in, he will be presented with (***( an input 
>box in which he can specify) search criteria ***(to limit the protected 
>pages to be displayed for his further action.)
>
>The default value of "*" requests all files. Currently, there are only
>
>a handful of protected pages or images so it is not overwhelming to
>
>request all files but as the system is used more ***(extensively), far too 
>many
>
>pages will be stored to show to superman everytime he examines the file 
>***(ie. page)
>
>list. If too many pages are found, superman's browser may crash since
>
>the resulting page could scroll down for thousands of pages and overrun
>
>his free system resources. Therefore, it makes sense to specify pattern
>
>matching criteria to determine which pages should be listed ***(for his 
>further action).
>
>(Para.)
>
>If a list of only those files stored in the image directory was desired, 
>superman
>
>could replace "*" with "/img/*" to show every file that has a PageName
>
>beginning with "/img/" (and is therefore stored in the server's image
>
>directory). Superman could specify multiple stars ("*") if he wanted a
>
>more complex search. Each star will match zero (0) or more characters
>
>of any kind.
>
>Having specified a search criteria of "*.htm*" to show a listing of all
>
>available HTML files and clicking "List Protected Pages", superman is
>
>shown a page containing a link at the top which goes back to the login
>
>page and a welcome message relating the validation of the newly
>
>allocated session code and the designated permission levels associated
>
>with his account (in this case: Read=0, Insert=0, Delete=0). Below
>
>those ***(a table is displayed) containing options ***(only) for each of 
>the files
>
>whose PageName matched his search criteria. Each of these HTML pages
>
>can be read, edited, or deleted (because superman's security levels allow 
>those permissions.)
>
>Clicking the button to read any particular page will ***(immediately 
>create) the page dynamically within a frame which ***(depicts) what the 
>entire page would look like if it were being viewed directly through 
>***(the current) dp.cgi. The edit option will enable superman to modify the 
>PageName, permission levels, or contents of any file. The delete
>
>option removes the file (right now, this is permanent, but I'm
>
>considering a trashcan scheme to make deletion less drastic). ****GOOD 
>IDEA) Why not write it up that way, but the trashcan must be for the 
>deleter only! I.e. password protected. Otherwise people could play with 
>deleted code and learn things. Right?
>
>Below the (matched--REMOVE) pages table, (which are being displayed 
>according to the match criteria,) is a small table which can be used to 
>create ***(totally) new files (for webpages or images or anything which can 
>be stored as a file). A PageName can be specified and a new empty file will 
>be created or superman could select a local file (from his own computer) to 
>upload to the server as the initial contents of the new file.
>
>This operation will fail if the file ***(name) already exists in the file 
>system or the
>
>database. If it exists in the database, it must first be deleted by a
>
>qualified user before a new file of the same name can be created. If
>
>the name is not in the database but is only found in the file system, an
>
>administrator of the server will have to remove the file (for security
>
>reasons) before it can be created.
>
>The table following contains user administration options. Superman
>
>could use the fields in the first row to create a new user in the system
>
>with initial values for their username, password, hint, permission
>
>levels, and session time limit. The next row can be used to update any
>
>user accout. New values can be provided to reset a user's forgotten
>
>password, reassign their hint or permission levels, specify another time
>
>limit, or lock/unlock the account. ***( I ASSUME THE FORMER INCUDES 
>RELEASING THE @$ HOUR HOLD. Perhaps you should say that. )
>
>The drop-down selection in the Username field describes each username, 
>permission levels, time limit, and locked status (U or L) all separated by 
>colons (:). The last row
>
>can be used to select a user to remove permanently from the system.
>
>The following button labeled "Change Group Settings" goes to a page
>
>which contains all of the defined group settings. This page can be used
>
>to create, modify, or delete definitions. When users login, each
>
>group is checked in order (top-down). The first group that contains a
>
>range which the user's permission levels ***(match or exceed) is the group 
>that the
>
>user is affiliated with (even if later groups also match). If a
>
>DefaultPage is specified for a user group, the protected page with the
>
>same PageName is displayed with dp.cgi after a login instead of the file
>
>list and administration options. Any number of groups can be created
>
>(limited by disk space) each with their own respective DefaultPage to
>
>which matching users will be ushered. The check boxes apply to users
>
>who match groups that don't have DefaultPages (because they have ***(a 
>permission level secure) enough to access ***(the file list and other 
>administrative features). Each
>
>box limits which components are displayed to logged-in members of that
>
>group.
>
>****(PIP AN EXAMPLE IS SORELY NEEDED HERE)
>
>The button below that labeled "Change Your Settings" goes to a screen
>
>for updating personal account settings. This can be used to change your
>
>password, hint, time limit, or search string. For superman to change
>
>his password, he'll have to supply his old one and then repeat the new
>
>one correctly (and it must be at least 4 characters) for the update to
>
>succeed. ****(PIP- Please make it 7 characters minimum)
>
>The last button is simply to "Logout".
>
>The above describes the administrative features of the 800Telephone
>
>system (as of June 28th). Below, I will describe the methods which can
>
>be used to embed database requests within html pages in order to produce
>
>secure dynamic pages. The system also has the ability to process
>
>embedded database insertions and updates from dynamic pages. ***(This code) 
>can be added to html files though the page edit option from the
>
>administrative list or directly on a workstation before being uploaded
>
>when a new PageName is created.
>
>There are currently two different ways to specify a database field to be
>
>dynamically inserted into html ***(by the server) each time the page is 
>accessed. The
>
>first method is just ***( abbreviated) cryptic code for describing any 
>field
>
>while the second is just a more verbose ***(and user friendly) method. 
>Functionally, the two are equivalent. In html, the first would look like:
>
>***(para.)
>
><h3>Some Field is: {id=1~Customer_Record.Type}</h3>
>
>where "id" is the name of the primary field and "1" is the primary value
>
>of the known record containing the desired field. "Customer_Record" is
>
>the name of the table that contains the field names "id" and "Type".
>
>"Type" is the desired field that gets replaced into the html (if
>
>permissions allow). An equivalent html line to the above with the
>
>second syntax method is:
>
>***(para)
>
><h3>Some Field 
>is:{PrimaryField{id}=PrimaryValue{1}~Database{demobase}.Table{Customer_Record}.DesiredField{Type}}</h3>
>
>***(Give an actual example)
>
>This second method must have each value enclosed in braces {}after the
>
>field name. The field names are: PrimaryField, PrimaryValue, Database,
>
>Table, and DesiredField. The Database field can be omitted for any
>
>normal query since the default value is the main 800Telephone database
>
>already (just as it was absent from the first example above but could be
>
>provided there also as another value preceeding the table name separated
>
>by a period).
>
>There are several operations which can be embedded within dynamic pages
>
>to update, modify, or delete data elements or records as well. Any
>
>number of these operations can be performed with a single submission.
>
>Examples for each follow.
>
>There may be several issues missing from the above description***(.) 
>(H)owever,
>
>it is my hope that an html/graphics designer could take ***(these 
>instructions) , along
>
>with a description of relevant database names and fields and a
>
>description of what inputs and outputs are necessary or desired for each
>
>particular page; ***(and only with these three elements would be able to 
>fully
>
>develop nearly all of the pages necessary for 800Telephone. ****(very 
>possible their are people that could do that, but of course that is not 
>what we envisioned in our agreement. The designers are only to provide 
>graphics. You may use the designers as a testing platform for our theories 
>and code to make it more readily apparent to web graphic designers.
>
>The method for updating data is relatively complex but it is a necessity
>
>of the inherent power involved in performing multiple secure database
>
>updates with each web form submission. The main processes available are
>
>insertions, updates, and deletions. To insert, the logged in user must
>
>have sufficient insert permissions. Sufficient delete permissions are
>
>required for deletes. The user must have both delete and insert
>
>permissions beyond the specified level for the data elements being
>
>modified to perform an updating operation. Any number of operations can
>
>be performed within a single form submission and each one is validated
>
>on an individual basis.
>
>***(It is anticipated that very little of the systems capabilities will be 
>used by an average customer. Suppliers may use more, but most of the 
>permissions are utilized by employees to utilize a browser based management 
>system over the internet anywhere in the world or their own Intranet to 
>totally run the enterprise.)
>
>
>
>****THE DISCRIPTION OF HOW TO USE THIS MAY BE OK FOR VERY BRIGHT DESIGNERS, 
>BUT MY INITAL REACTION IS IT NEEDS SOME SIMPLIFICATION-PERHAPS PULL DOWN 
>BOXES OR A FRONT END. WE CAN DISCUSS IT IN PERSON.
>
>Each suboperation is ***(automatically??) encoded with operation numbers in 
>each name field.
>
>Listed ***(hereafter) is an example of a simple insertion:
>
><form action="dp.cgi" method="post">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich0bas" value="demobase">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich0tbl" value="Customer_Record">
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld0" value="Type"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut0val0" value=""><br>
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld1" value="Reason"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut0val1" value=""><br>
>
><input type="hidden" name="wut0todo" value="insereco">
>
><input type="hidden" name="pagename" value="customer0.htm">
>
><input type="submit" name="submit" value="Create New Record"></form>
>
>The (currently) available values for the hidden field "wut$Xtodo" (where
>
>$X = the operation number, 0 in this case) are "insereco", "updtfiel",
>
>and "delereco". Operation numbers begin at 0 (zero) and proceed
>
>sequentially (in decimal notation) upwards unbounded. One submission
>
>button could perform any number of inserts, updates, and deletes as long
>
>as each is encoded sequentially according to the operation number. To
>
>perform any insert, the following fields are required:
>
>* "pagename" is a required field for every submitted form to tell
>
>which dynamic page to load after the submission is processed.
>
>(NOTE: When only pagename is specified, it's just like a normal
>
>link to the new dynamic page without any database changes.)
>
>* "wich$Xbas" must contain the name of the database into which data
>
>will be inserted.
>
>* "wich$Xtbl" is the table to receive the inserted data.
>
>* "wut$Xtodo" must contain "insereco" for an insertion.
>
>* "wut$Xfld$Y" is the name of the field you wish to provide an initial
>
>value for where the integer $Y ascends from 0 to the number of
>
>fields you wish to insert into the new record.
>
>* "wut$Xval$Y" is the corresponding value to insert into the specified
>
>database and table and field. (NOTE: Any number of field and
>
>value pairs can be specified up to the total number of fields
>
>specified within the table. Each value will be given a default
>
>if no entry for the field is designated.)
>
>To perform an update, the following fields are required:
>
>* "pagename" to specify which page to load after the update is
>
>performed.
>
>* "wich$Xbas" must contain the name of the database from which data
>
>will be updated.
>
>* "wich$Xtbl" is the table to receive the data update.
>
>* "wut$Xtodo" must contain "updtfiel" for an update.
>
>* "nown$Xfld" is the name of the field (most likely the name of the
>
>primary key) which identifies the record you wish to update.
>
>* "nown$Xval" is the value of the field which is a unique
>
>identification value for the record you wish to update.
>
>* "wut$Xfld$Y" is the name of the field you wish to provide a new
>
>value for where the integer $Y ascends from 0 to the number of
>
>fields you wish to insert into the new record.
>
>* "wut$Xval$Y" is the corresponding value to update in the specified
>
>database and table and field. (NOTE: Any number of field and
>
>value pairs can be specified up to the total number of fields
>
>specified within the table. Each value will be retain it's
>
>original value if no entry for the field is specified.)
>
>To perform a delete, the following fields are required:
>
>* "pagename" to specify which page to load after the update is
>
>performed.
>
>* "wich$Xbas" must contain the name of the database from which the
>
>data record will be removed.
>
>* "wich$Xtbl" is the table to delete the data from.
>
>* "wut$Xtodo" must contain "delereco" for an update.
>
>* "nown$Xfld" is the name of the field (most likely the name of the
>
>primary key) which identifies the record you wish to delete.
>
>* "nown$Xval" is the value of the field which is a unique
>
>identification value for the record you wish to delete.
>
>Following is an exceptionally simple example of an insert, update and
>
>delete all in a single form:
>
><form action="dp.cgi" method="post">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich0bas" value="demobase">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich0tbl" value="Customer_Record">
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld0" value="Type"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut0val0" value=""><br>
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld1"
>
>value="RelationshipXq"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut0val1" value=""><br>
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld2" value="Reason"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut0val2" value=""><br>
>
><input type="hidden" name="wut0todo" value="insereco">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich1bas" value="demobase">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich1tbl" value="Customer_Record">
>
>Known Field?: <input type="text" name="nown1fld" value="id"><br>
>
>Known Value?: <input type="text" name="nown1val" value="3"><br>
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch1fld0" value="Type"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut1val0" value=""><br>
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch1fld1"
>
>value="RelationshipXq"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut1val1" value=""><br>
>
>Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch1fld2" value="Reason"><br>
>
>What Value?: <input type="text" name="wut1val2" value=""><br>
>
><input type="hidden" name="wut1todo" value="updtfiel">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich2bas" value="demobase">
>
><input type="hidden" name="wich2tbl" value="Customer_Record">
>
>Known Primary Field?: <input type="text" name="nown2fld" value="id"><br>
>
>Which Unique Value?: <input type="text" name="nown2val" value="5"><br>
>
><input type="hidden" name="wut2todo" value="delereco">
>
><input type="hidden" name="pagename" value="customer0.htm">
>
><input type="submit" name="submit" value="Return to Primary Customer
>
>Page With A Record Creation, Update, & Delete all at once!">
>
></form>
>
>Hopefully the above description is clear enough to describe the method
>
>of my madness... I mean my genius =) If you have questions, feel free
>
>to pay me to answer them. The remaining operation is a way to perform
>
>selections (searches) on the database in order to arrange comparisons
>
>and statistical evaluations generated from large portions of data. I
>
>will update this description once selections are operational and can be
>
>described. TTFN.
>
>-Pip
>

>         "Just-Copy-It" Installation!
>       (Traditional installation not required)--
>
>
>--------------------------------------------------------------------------
>
>       Follow these simple steps to effect BrowserExpress' capabilities on 
>your organization's server:
>
>         a.. Step 1. Extract the distribution files into a temporary 
>location.
>
>       Download BrowserExpress
>--------------------------------------------------------------------------
>
>       System Requirements:
>
>         a.. Linux, Unix, or Windows NT
>         b.. Web Server
>         c.. 1 MB Disk Space
>
>--------------------------------------------------------------------------
>
>       Client Requirements:
>       Noneuse any browser with an Internet connection
>      a.. Step 2. Copy BrowserExpress.exe or BrowserExpress.cgi, and 
>BrowserExpress.ini to the location on your Web Server that has execution 
>enabled. Also, if you are running the evaluation copy of BrowserExpress you 
>must write enable BrowserExpress.ini. Once you run BrowserExpress the first 
>time you may reset the BrowserExpress.ini file attribute to Read-only.
>           a.. NT Version -- The default location on IIS v4.0 is 
>"C:\Inetpub\scripts". Don't forget to ensure that the BrowserExpress.ini 
>file attribute is not set to Read-only.
>
>           b.. Linux/Unix Version -- The default location on Apache v1.3.9 
>is /home/httpd/cgi-bin or /usr/local/www/cgi-bin. Don't forget to "chmod +x 
>BrowserExpress.cgi" when you get BrowserExpress.cgi in the appropriate 
>directory. Also, don't forget to "chmod o+w BrowserExpress.ini."
>
>
>         b.. Step 3. Step 3 Copy MyLogo.gif to the root directory of your 
>Default Web Site.
>           a.. NT Version -- The default location on IIS v4.0 is 
>C:\Inetpub\wwwroot.
>           b.. Linux/Unix Version -- The default location on Apache v1.3.9 
>is /home/httpd/html or /usr/local/www/data.
>
>
>         c.. Step 4. Give your users a URL that points them to the Server 
>on which BrowserExpress resides, e.g., 
>"www.mycompany.com/scripts/BrowserExpress.exe" or 
>"www.mycompany.com/cgi-bin/BrowserExpress.cgi".
>
>
>         d.. Step 5. Modify the appropriate portions in the 
>BrowserExpress.ini file, as explained in the installation manual.
>
>
>         e.. Step 6. If you wish to display your logo or banner 
>advertisement within the user interface, replace "MyLogo.gif" with your 
>logo filename. Ensure your logo is in GIF format. To help you size your 
>logo, the "MyLogo" is displayed with "width=120" and "height=101." The logo 
>width and height are customizable.
>       Use BrowserExpress to your full advantage thereafter.
>
>

>      E-Commerce Solutions: Template-Driven Pages
>             Jun 28, 2000, 13 :40 UTC (7 Talkback[s]) (1786 reads) (Other 
>stories by Martin C. Brown)
>
>
>       By Martin C. Brown
>
>       The basis of all web sites is HTML, and that HTML is used to 
>implement your design. There are other elements of course, graphics, and 
>presumably the dynamic content of your site, but the backbone of your site 
>will be it's design and layout. Now, I'm no expert on design--I can do a 
>technical drawing, but ask me to come up with a logo and then draw it, and 
>I'm suddenly lost. We'll therefore ignore the design issue, and instead 
>concentrate on the implementation!
>
>       Producing any kind of Web site, and e-commerce ones in particular, 
>you are likely to be following a very simple layout using consistent 
>elements like toolbars or navigation bars to help guide your users around 
>your site. There are different ways of getting round the problems of these 
>constant elements, frequently frames are used for this purpose, and the new 
>CSS (Cascading Style Sheets) can be used to similar effect. I've even seen 
>some complex sites that use JavaScript to build sections of the page 
>dynamically.
>
>       However, for an E-Commerce site there are extra complications, most 
>of time you'll be building sections of the page dynamically based on 
>searches, user selections and preferences.
>
>       Before we get on to the complexities of dynamically driven sites, 
>lets go back a step and look at a template-driven site that uses Server 
>Side Includes (SSI) to build up the pages. Understanding the basics of SSI 
>will help us to understand how to use and employ templates in just but 
>about solution. We'll use my writing website, www.mcwords.com, which was 
>actually designed with SSI specifically in mind as our example.
>
>       The home page looks like this:
>
>
>
>       Whilst the actual to build that page is short and sweet:
>
><HTML>
><HEAD>
><TITLE>MCwords</TITLE>
><!--#include virtual="/ssi/topbar.html" -->
><table border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=0 width=100%>
><tr>
><td width="66%" valign=top>
><table border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=2 width=100%>
><!--#include virtual="/ssi/mainnewspanel.shtml" -->
><!--#include virtual="/archive/summary.html" -->
></table>
></td>
><td width="34%" valign=top>
><table width="100%" border=0 cellspacing=0 cellpadding=2>
><!--#include virtual="/ssi/updatepanel.html" -->
><!--#include virtual="/ssi/downloadpanel.html" -->
><!--#include virtual="/ssi/dreamhostad.html" -->
></table>
></td>
></tr>
></table>
><!--#include virtual="/ssi/tagline.html" -->
>
>       Aside from some minor formatting, the bulk of the code is actually 
>taken up by SSI include directives which import the main logo and top 
>navigation panel, the body section, a side section and the trailing 
>information. In essence what we've got here is a page made up of five 
>distinct sections, the surrounding template gives us our base-the page 
>title and main table, whilst the imported sections handle everything else.
>
>       Configuring Apache
>       For this to work correctly, you need to have Apache configured first 
>to handle SSI, and then to use the index.shtml file as a default. This is 
>fairly straightforward. To enable SSI, enable the Includes directive on a 
>directory:
>
><Directory /usr/local/http/webs/mcwords>
>         Options +Includes
></Directory>
>
>       Then tell Apache which files to parse for SSI commands. The general 
>consensus is to use files with an extension of .shtml, which you configure 
>like this:
>
>AddType text/html .shtml
>AddHandler server-parsed .shtml
>
>       Finally, you need to update the DirectoryIndex option:
>
>DirectoryIndex index.shtml index.html
>       Element Design
>       Our sample page is actually duplicated across the entire site, I use 
>the sample basic template and just change the include directive to include 
>the information I want. Aside from the obvious benefits of the things like 
>a consistent top bar, I can also use the same body elements and sidebar 
>elements in other pages. For example the main heading page news items can 
>be used as introductory panels for the individual sections and so on.
>
>       For E-Commerce sites you can employ the same basic tactics for 
>search fields, control panels and even product information, although it's 
>more likely that will be driven from a scripting language than static HTML. 
>We'll actually look at techniques for introducing dynamic elements through 
>our templates in moment.
>
>       The trick to handling all of this effectively is to create each 
>included element and as a standalone component. That way the element is 
>both standalone--in that it could be displayed essentially on its own 
>without any further window dressing--and able to be integrated without 
>needing any other files or window dressing to make it work.
>
>       For example, take the panel on the right; this is a single table 
>cell, which itself has an embedded table. The "Recent Site Updates" will be 
>a new row of that table, so the code looks like this:
>
><tr>
><td width=5>&nbsp;</td>
><td bgcolor="#ff0000" align=center><font face="Arial,Helvetica" 
>color="#ffffff"><b>Recent Site Updates</b></font></td>
></tr>
><tr>
><td width=5>&nbsp;</td>
><td>
>Learn more about your iMac with <a 
>href="/projects/books/imac/index.shtml">iMac FYI</a><br>
>Perl AA <a href="/downloads/paa/index.shtml">Scripts Updated</a><Br>
>Get the info on <a href="/projects/books/pyaa/index.shtml">Python Annotated 
>Archives</a><Br>
>Check out <a href="/projects/books/ptcr/index.shtml">Perl: The Complete 
>Reference</a><Br>
>Download <a href="/downloads/paa/PAA04Sample.pdf">Perl AA Ch 4</a> Free! 
>(PDF, 540k)<Br>
></td>
></tr>
>
>       That's everything--the new table row, the header for the section, 
>and the body, as well as the trailing HTML code to close those elements 
>off. This keeps the clutter and management of the elements out of the main 
>files and instead inside the individual components.
>
>       Producing Your Design
>       The easiest way to design your site when producing a system like 
>this is to actually create a static page--or series of pages if you are 
>using frames--and then try to logically split that up.
>
>       Once you have the individual elements, then optimize them to keep 
>the sizes down to a minimum (this helps your server and your prospective 
>clients). Finally, use the final version to produce templates that can then 
>be duplicated and used for all the different includes that you need to make 
>your site.
>
>       How you design and layout your site is entirely up to you, and 
>really an HTML, not Apache, issue, so I'll leave that as an exercise for 
>the reader.
>
>       Directory Organization
>       Just before we look at some of the funkier things you can do with 
>SSI and template driven pages, it's worth just covering the basics of your 
>directory layout. On my site, I have a single directory at the top level 
>called ssi, this contains all of the core components like the top bar, 
>bottom tag line and the main panels on the right hand side. The main body 
>of the content is then taken from the corresponding directories.
>
>       Although this kind of layout is not particularly unique or clever, 
>it does make the whole process a lot easier. It also ensures that I can 
>easily identify the elements that I want to include. This will become 
>particularly important as we start to embed different elements through our 
>script engines.
>
>       Quasi-Dynamic Content
>       Up to now, we've strictly been dealing with static pages. Although 
>it's possible that some of your content will be static based, it's highly 
>unlikely that your entire site will be able to make direct use of SHTML 
>pages. We'll be looking at how to build entirely script-driven sites that 
>employ templates in the next article. Until then, we can actually introduce 
>some further dynamic content without resorting to a full script.
>
>       Using the exec SSI directive we can execute a CGI script instead of 
>embedding a static HTML file. Most sites actually use this feature to 
>include a site counter, but it can be used in any situation where you want 
>some dynamic content. On my site I've used this as a way of introducing 
>some random elements into the various side panels that would otherwise have 
>to be manually selected on each page.
>
>       The script is pretty simple; it only has to select a file from a 
>predefined list and then open and send it back. Because the script is still 
>parsed by the server though it does need to output an appropriate header. 
>You can see the script below:
>
>#!/usr/local/bin/perl
>print "Content-type: text/html\n\n";
>
>@opts = qw/paa imac beos/;
>
>$chosen = $opts[rand(@opts)];
>
>open(FILE,'/usr/local/http/webs/mcwords/ssi/'
>           . $chosen . 'buypanel.html');
>while(<FILE>)
>{
>     print;
>}
>close(FILE);
>
>       This is not a suitable solution however for anything more complex 
>than embedding a flat script, we can't supply arguments, and the request 
>isn't made in the same way as calling a CGI from the client. Still, we're 
>beginning to get the basis of a dynamic template-driven environment.
>
>       The Next Step
>       The basics applied in this article will work with any 
>template-driven system. In every system, from SSI to a Perl, Python or 
>other script driven solution the aim of templates is to centralize the 
>HTML. That makes developing and updating the site easier--you only have to 
>change one file--and it also provides consistency across the entire site.
>
>       In the next article we'll move on and see how we can use different 
>scripting engines and the same basic template principles. We'll also look 
>at parsed templates, as opposed to the static templates we've seen in this 
>article.
>
>       Martin C. Brown is a full-time writer and consultant specializing in 
>multiplatform integration and internet technologies. He is author of both 
>the Perl and Python Annotated Archives and Perl The Complete Reference.

>                   SITE DESCRIPTIONS
>
>
>      Apache Guide: Advanced SSI Techniques
>             Jun 26, 2000, 04 :00 UTC (5 Talkback[s]) (2168 reads) (Other 
>stories by Rich Bowen)
>
>
>       This is the third in a three-article series about Server Side 
>Includes, or SSI. In the first article, I discussed configuring your Apache 
>server to permit SSI. In the second article, I gave some examples of how 
>you might use SSI to add dynamic content to your web pages. In this 
>article, I'll talk about some of the advanced features available with 
>Server Side Includes.
>
>       (Note: Most of the features discussed in this article are only 
>available to you if you are running Apache 1.2 or later. Of course, if you 
>are not running Apache 1.2 or later, you need to upgrade immediately, if 
>not sooner. Go on. Do it now. We'll wait.)
>
>       Setting Variables
>       Using the set attribute, you can set variables for later use. We'll 
>need this later in the discussion, so we'll talk about this here. The 
>syntax of this is as follows:
>
>         <!--#set var="name" value="Rich" -->
>       In addition to merely setting values literally like that, you can 
>use any other variable, including, for example, environment variables, or 
>some of the variables we discussed in the last article (like LAST_MODIFIED, 
>for example) to give values to your variables. You will specify that 
>something is a variable, rather than a literal string, by using the dollar 
>sign ($) before the name of the variable:
>
>        <!--#set var="modified" value="$LAST_MODIFIED" -->
>       To put a literal dollar sign into the value of your variable, you 
>need to escape the dollar sign with a backslash:
>
>        <!--#set var="cost" value="\$100" -->
>       Finally, if you want to put a variable in the midst of a longer 
>string, and there's a chance that the name of the variable will run up 
>against some other characters, and thus be confused with those characters, 
>you can place the name of the variable in braces, to remove this confusion. 
>(It's hard to come up with a really good example of this, but hopefully 
>you'll get the point.) To wit:
>
>        <!--#set var="date" value="${DATE_LOCAL}_${DATE_GMT}" -->
>       Conditional Expressions
>       Now that we have variables and are able to set and compare their 
>values, we can use them to express conditionals. This lets SSI be a tiny 
>programming languages of sorts. mod_include provides an if, elif, else, 
>endif structure for building conditional statements. This allows you to 
>effectively generate multiple logical pages out of one actual page.
>
>       The structure of this conditional construct is:
>
>     <!--#if expr="test_condition" -->
>     <!--#elif expr="test_condition" -->
>     <!--#else -->
>     <!--#endif -->
>       A test_condition can be any sort of logical comparison--either 
>comparing values to one another, or testing the "truth" of a particular 
>value. (A given string is true if it is nonempty.) For a full list of the 
>comparison operators available to you, see the mod_include documentation. 
>Here are some examples of how one might use this construct.
>
>       In your configuration file, you could put the following line:
>
>         BrowserMatchNoCase macintosh Mac
>         BrowserMatchNoCase MSIE InternetExplorer
>       This will set environment variables Mac and InternetExplorer to 
>true, if the client is running Internet Explorer on a Macintosh.
>
>       Then, in your SSI-enabled document, you might do the following:
>
>         <!--#if expr="${Mac} && ${InternetExplorer} -->
>         Apologetic text goes here
>         <!--#else -->
>         Cool JavaScript code goes here
>         <!--#endif -->
>       Not that I have anything against IE on Macs--I just struggled for a 
>few hours last week trying to get some JavaScript working on IE on a Mac, 
>when it was working everywhere else. The above was the interim workaround.
>
>       Any other variable (either ones that you define, or normal 
>enviroment variables) can be used in conditional statements. With Apache's 
>ability to set environment variables with the SetEnvIf directives, and 
>other related directives, this functionality can let you do some pretty 
>involved dynamic stuff without ever resorting to CGI.
>
>       Conclusion
>       SSI is certainly not a replacement for CGI, or other technologies 
>used for generating dynamic web pages. But it is certainly a great way to 
>add small amounts of dynamic content to pages, without doing a lot of extra 
>work.
>
>       See the docs on mod_include for more information on using SSI.

>From: "Len Fish" <leonard3@home.com>
>To: "PIP TIGGER(2)" <piptigger@hotmail.com>
>Subject: Transactional data bases
>Date: Sat, 15 Apr 2000 10:46:41 -0700
>
>
>Do you know that many sql databases are transactional. That is if a 
>transaction that posts several tables fails, it automatically reverses out 
>all entries in that transaction.
>
>MySQL does not have that feature. It is an "atomic" data base, as opposed 
>to transactional. Postgre is transactional and also free. SQL7 and Oracle I 
>believe are transactional.
>
>Please make certain that we have, or OM has written that important 
>capability, as we ARE transactional.
>
>Your responses would be appreciated.
>
>Len

> > cookie.  If no cookie is found, the available items are displayed for

> > demonstration uses a 'favorite animal' cookie, but this could easily be
> > modified to fit your needs.
