April 25

Len,
I did not start arguing with you.  I did not agree to any previous proposal 
(other than $32/hr for my services).  You have never offered me $500 per 
week.  You insult my integrity and my loyalty at every opportunity but I 
have not been deficient in either.  I'm afraid your perception of the past 
events does not coincide with mine so I thought it might be helpful if I 
relate what has happened so far from my perspective:
1) You agreed to hire me for $32 / hour to write code for you.
2) You did not have any development environment so (after significant 
discussion) I recommended that you establish your own server.  You had me 
perform cost analysis and make recommendations and phone calls to price 
several differing server options.  (Since this isn't coding, maybe it isn't 
considered work according to our initial agreement but it definitely was 
something I wouldn't have done in my free time and it was certainly job 
related research/analysis based on my hardware experience/expertise)
3) We ventured to local electronics stores for further server hardware 
options, operating system software, and reference materials.
4) You decided to purchase a computer that was not designed to be a server 
at all which came installed with Windows98.  You also bought RedHat 6.2 
separately.
5) The network card in the Windows98 computer you bought did not work with 
Linux so I gave you mine.
6) We installed RedHat and I configured the network settings, server 
software, and user permissions.
7) You took your old hub back and gave me a new one the next day (which 
works fine... Thank you).
8) I downloaded, installed, and correctly configured MySQL onto the server.
9) We discussed the possibility that I develop the entire backend to the 
800Telephone system myself.
10) You asked how much I need to live and I replied "$500/wk" which I 
quickly followed with the qualification that even though I could live off so 
little money, that doesn't mean I would like to.  My objective was not to 
get payed as little as possible to do as much work as possible.  I have been 
and am glad to work hard to be nicely paid.
11) We discussed the possibility of $1000/wk. which sounded much closer to 
what I'd like to be paid (compared to the minimum I could afford to live 
on).  You stipulated that you would pay that rate for 10 weeks and that I'd 
be obligated to complete the project for free if it required more time.  You 
also suggested that you'd keep me busy for the entire 10 weeks if I finished 
early.
12) We made no official agreement.  No proposal was written down in any way.
13) I needed to examine the requirements of the project before I could begin 
to determine my ability to complete it.
14) I needed to determine my ability to complete the project before I could 
possibly arrive at a reasonable or exact completion time frame.
15) I reviewed the documents last night and replied today (as I said I 
would) with my concerns; the biggest of which was the possibility that the 
project would require more than 10 weeks to complete and that I would have 
to work for free to complete it.
16) You replied upset with me as though I had gone and changed the agreement 
after shaking your hand on some specific deal to complete the project for 
you (which I never did).  I've been as clear and fair and direct with you as 
I can possibly be.  I haven't promised more than I could deliver and I've 
already demonstrated competence in areas that you did not anticipate when 
you initially hired me (namely my ability to evaluate server-related 
hardware options, to setup and configure server software, to administrate a 
server, and to develop databases)
17) I replied and explained that I hadn't agreed to anything regarding 
developing all of the 800Telephone system (despite what you may have 
thought) because I wasn't ever equipped to do so since I had never read what 
the system needed to do before last night.
18) You replied that we are arguing and that you've been doing me favors all 
along and I haven't seen it that way and that I can get $750/wk for as long 
as it takes or $10k for the whole job and that programmers are terrible to 
deal with because of their one-way aspirations

...which basically brings us up to date...
Now... you know I wanted to work for no less than $32/hr from the outset of 
our relationship.  The two offers you seem to have made me are basically 
$10k for work that may take longer than 10 weeks or $750 / week for as long 
as it takes.  Now if we consider these two possibilities, it seems clear 
that you are not interested in paying me what we initially agreed to 
($32/hr) even if I am more valuable than a simple coder to you.  Let us say 
that a 10k contract is signed and work is completed in 10 weeks... that 
works out to $25/hr. if I only work 40 hours per week... in all likelihood, 
I would work nearly twice that making my hourly rate somewhere near $15/hr.  
If the job were to take longer than 10 weeks (and therefore I have to finish 
the remainder without any further compensation), clearly this hourly rate 
would come closer to $10/hr.  When I try to explain to you that I don't want 
to be payed so little for my future efforts, you retaliate with your second 
option of $750/wk. and insults toward the programming community in general.  
I have not been trying to pull a fast one on you here.  You wanted to hire 
me and every opportunity you get, you try to get me to agree to be payed as 
little as possible.  Maybe you don't realize you're doing this.  Maybe you 
do intend to pay me as little as possible to limit your own business costs.  
I don't know which it is but let me make things as clear as I can:
  I can afford to live off $500 / wk.
  I can make at least $500 / wk. doing data entry or web design almost 
anywhere.
  I will not be happy making $500 / wk (~$12.50/hr.).
  $1000 / wk. (~$25/hr.) is still less than I would like to make.
  Technical experience similar to mine often goes for $45+/hr. today.
  I have asked to be payed at least $32/hr.

Now I see three basic options for our business relationship in the future:
  1) You pay me $480 ($32/hr. x 15 hours) for the work I have done for you 
thus far and we both go our separate ways.
  2) You pay me $32/hr. to continue to work for you and my responsibilities 
can include administration of your server, database design and 
implementation, Perl/CGI coding, and OpenMerchant configuration/enhancement 
development.  I could be very similar to a direct employee devoted to 
constructing whatever you need and want as quickly and completely as I am 
able.
  3) You treat me more like a distant programming firm hired to develop the 
underlying code for your entire 800Telephone system.  If this is the 
arrangement, then (after further deliberations) we may agree that the entire 
project is worth $10k and that total development time can span no longer 
than 10 weeks.  That would also mean that completion of the project in less 
than 10 weeks still entitles me to the full price stipulated in the contract 
($10k).

These are the only three options that seem fair to me.  Please choose one of 
them when you have time or comment if none are adequate for you.  Thanks.  
TTFN & Shalom.

-Pip

p.s. I have removed users "vijay" and "test" from the server as per your 
request.

June 1

Hey Len,
I just wanted to give you an update on my progress.  After the preliminary 
testing on Tue. and a stronger one yesterday afternoon, it became apparent 
that security concerns (in regards to database access) hadn't been 
sufficiently addressed.  I thought of ways to circumvent the security 
measures originally developed.  I researched and read for almost 2 hours 
last night about CGI security methods and special procedures for state 
retention.  I originally had the permissions residing within the same 
database as the rest of the data (these permissions determine who can access 
anything whatsoever from databases to users to actual data records to 
files).  Last night I designed two solutions and after much consideration, I 
decided on one and began coding it (to be more secure this time around).  
That's what I'm working on right now.  Previously, with some creative html 
submission, users could override their own permission level and with that 
access, simply set their permissions higher which would enable everything to 
be compromised.  The new design basically segregates each level according to 
how damaging a security breach could be.  This means that basically only the 
super user can access the database and user permission tables.  I've also 
had to add a new criterion for testing which enables partial creations.  
This has taken a lot of time since all the code tests need to reflect this 
new field too and it's not behaving properly just yet.  This new structure 
should prove much more reliable and secure.  I'm planning to get this all 
done by tonight (hopefully bugs fixed too).  I've also done some server 
maintenance while you were gone which removed the openmerchant virtual host 
and other settings which were involved with the development version of that. 
  I've left most of the files on the server (in case we can benefit from 
their code or data structures etc.) but I've removed them from the apache 
configuration and cleaned up the web server operation methods.  I've also 
looked at Dynamic.net this week to see if we could setup 
len@800telephone.com (& pip@800 etc.)through them and it seems that all of 
their email packages cost money and aren't included with most of the hosting 
options.  If you were emailed special instructions on what services are 
included with our hosting package or how to specifically setup email 
aliases, please forward them to me so I can make more progress on that 
front.  I read and fiddled for a while with how to setup the required email 
services directly from the 800tele server but I didn't get a chance to 
configure them completely because I'm still not quite sure where all the 
proper settings files are and even if I could get them working perfectly 
right now (probably with forwarding from len@800 to leonard3@home etc.), it 
would be useless since mail sent to an @800tele address will be going to 
dynamic.net until they alias to our server or we can configure theirs to 
forward directly.  Once the mail could get through, I'll work on it more 
diligently but I couldn't justify spending more than an hour or two on it 
this week since I can't test it yet and it won't work until dynamic is setup 
for the addresses anyway.  I've had a lot of other code on my mind too.  
I've finally gotten my harddrives working correctly without creating SCSI 
bus errors.  I'd be coding on my floor computer while the other one was 
formatting the 18GB drive (for almost 2 hours) which had to be done 3 times 
before it would actually take an Operating System installation.  Now my main 
computer is running solidly (with the case cover on and everything) and so 
is the floor one.  I've gotten a ton done this week.  I don't have too much 
more before this ModifyMySQL module is working with the new design and is 
actually safe from cracking (or at least far more secure than the original). 
  Of course I'd like to have a testable version of it late this afternoon or 
early this evening.  If I get such a version up (that's not frighteningly 
buggy), I'll send you another email with a link to it.  Anyway, this is what 
I've been doing and what I'm working on now.  I hope your trip was as good 
as possible.  Talk to you soon.  TTFN & Shalom.

-Pip

during the peak cable modem usage saturation times during most evenings.

coding while listening to certain mp3 radio stations.  I code with usually 7

June 15

Hello Len.  I wanted to send an update before I head off to the airport.  
I've been werking all night and this is what I did:
  I got all subdirectories in PageNames to work correctly (that is with or 
without a / before the path)
  I made a very special public clause for protected files that have a 
PageName which begins with img/ or /img/ so that they can be placed in a 
folder specifically for graphics and referencable from any html document on 
the server (including other dynamic ones which is really the whole point).
  I extended the default PageName functionality so that if none is supplied 
and a local file is selected for upload (when creating a new protected file 
on the server), it extracts the local file name for use as the server's 
PageName.
  I also enabled detection of .gif or .jpg as default upload files so that 
they automatically get /img/ prepended so that they will automatically be 
accessible as graphics for other pages.  To make uploaded graphics 
inaccessible, you must supply a PageName when uploading that does not begin 
with img/ or /img/.
  I further debugged the transition from ' in the dynamic accesses over to ~ 
(accent to tilde).
  I completed the ability for any user to change their hint or password 
online securely (with all the redundancy and correct error messages etc.).
  I fixed a bug with the password timeout which would allow create and 
delete functionality to circumvent the idle period limitations.
  I corrected the hostname setting on the server in preparation for the 
repointing of the domain.
  I adjusted the date and time which are local to the server so that the 
timed lockout test can be accurate.  The server was defaulted to some time 
last year and a few hours off before so they should be correct now.
  I wrote portions of user and permission level alteration code so that 
database updates (for users, permissions, and end-customer-bound data 
tables) can be updated securely.
  I was werking on secure data update/insert and user 
security/administration functions when it became apparent that a particular 
Perl module would be helpful for database integration (Data::DataTables).  
When retrieving this module (which is relatively small and should have been 
a quick installation), the installation utility detected that a newer 
version of Perl was available and automatically proceeded to download and 
install that.  Our original version of Perl was something like 5.0.0.3 and 
the newest one (which was just released a week or two ago IIRC) is version 
5.6.  This began at around 4:00am and ran for nearly half an hour.  When it 
completed, the server stopped responding (and presumably hard-crashed).  I 
haven't been able to access the development server since (through http, 
telnet, or ftp).  I've been trying to write more code locally but I have had 
no way to test anything for the past two hours.  I've tried to probe the 
server numerous times hoping that it isn't totally locked up but it hasn't 
responded.  I must leave for the LAX in less than 1 hour.  I've accomplished 
everything I could tonight.  Hopefully we can resolve the server problem 
promptly when I return next week.  I wasn't doing anything anomolous tonight 
nor the other time the server crashed.  If the filesystem indeed needs to be 
rebuilt again, I think it is apparent that the hardware components in the 
development server are sub-par and should be replaced with higher quality 
equipment.  The most likely culprits of such recurring failures would be (in 
order of likelihood) a poorly manufactured hard drive, defective IDE cables, 
faulty memory modules (RAM), or a deficient disk controller (EIDE) on the 
motherboard.  Hopefully the problem did not result in filesystem corruption 
as it did last time so the repair can be quick and painless.  Anita should 
be able to construct pages (based on what we discussed earlier this week) to 
display content for preliminary html documents like the touchtone and 
product category pages.  Those can be developed locally on her workstation 
until we can re-establish access to the development server.  I really am 
amazed that this happened just before I'm leaving and have been hoping that 
the server would come back up but it doesn't look like that's happening.  
I'll probably be in touch on Tuesday as soon as I can wake up.  Have a good 
weekend if possible.  TTFN & Shalom.

-PipTigger

p.s. Please forward this to Anita or fill her in as to the changes that have 
been made in the system so that the briefing next week can be brief.  I was 
going to cc this mail to her but I realized that it might contain some 
things that you wouldn't want her to see so I figured you can determine 
that.  If you would like, next week I'll distill this email down to just the 
details of the system changes as they pertain to her and making pages in 
general.  Let me know.  Thanks.

Hey Len.
    I've had a hideous time with DBI tonight.  I thought all I'd have to do 
to be up and running again was to restart the MySQL server but that didn't 
work and I've tried a ton of widely varied things to get it to run.  After 
many failed attempts at configuring different modules and reading many help 
texts on the subject, I recompiled MySQL and Perl5.6 directly from online 
source code archives in order to obtain coherent binary versions which 
dynamically link to common (and compatible) components.  Last week's crash 
ruined some dependencies which couldn't be easily reconstructed.  I 
installed the latest DBI and finally configured, tested, and installed the 
correct drivers for MySQL to interface with DBI.  All of the components are 
operational and all the old code is (finally) running again.
    I've saved the source code to the transactional enhancement to MySQL 
that you pointed me to however, I have been inspecting it for the past half 
hour and their online documentation and I've realized that it would not be a 
simple solution for us at this point.  They have their own modules to 
interface with MySQL called Berkeley DB & DB_FILE which are significantly 
different from DBI.  Their modules for MySQL are only in an experimental 
stage right now so they are not even as developed as DBI's driver.  
Basically, much of the database code would need to be rewritten if we wanted 
to utilize Berkeley DB instead of DBI to access MySQL.  I'm really tired so 
I may not think the task is so daunting once I check it out more thoroughly 
(and clear-headedly) tomorrow but it seems like it would be a ton of extra 
work to get their transactional layer implemented into our system.
    I've tried to work further on the secure data update (now that the 
database is accessible again) so that I can get that running and then 
section off a stable demo with all of the secure core functions in place so 
that we can have a nice demo... but I'm nodding off because the sun is up 
and I've been pounding my head against the server configuration all night.  
I'm trying to stay awake to get more done before I fall asleep but I wanted 
to send you this email to let you know what has happened and that I'll 
probably wake up around 1 or 2 pm so I'll give you a call then.  TTFN.

-Pip

p.s. Now, at least we have the latest versions of all the software involved.

The new version of Perl was of a different binary compatibility.  It was 
updated automatically while installing another module.  Most users don't 
encounter such difficulties but we have better versions of Perl and MySQL 
now that we've compiled them specifically for our machine.  These files are 
unrelated to the backup I sent to Matt.  The code I've written hasn't 
changed but the libraries they expect to be able to link to became 
unavailable and needed to be reinstalled and configured correctly and it's 
not an easy task.  I didn't expect to need the source code to Perl or to 
have to configure the MySQL code to be able to compile an entirely new 
binary for our purposes since I could not have forseen the automatic 
incompatibility in binaries.  Now that I know, I can go ahead and include 
both of those 5MB source files in the next archive (mushrooming it's size 
over 10 times the original).  It's not really smart to do something like 
that though because it really doesn't save you any time to save large source 
files when there are constantly released newer versions online and any 
reconfiguration of the server would require the server to be online, 
therefore, it will (almost always) make most sense to re-retrieve large 
files needed for server configuration each time you find yourself 
configuring a server so that you can get the most recent ones and because 
there would be a negligable advantage (speed or convenience-wise) by having 
large config files archived on some other PC rather than re-getting the 
files from the code author's archive.  You want to backup a lot of things 
but until we can really backup everything, there are going to be many 
modules which don't make sense to store copies of regularly because when we 
need them again, I'm not going to use the archived ones anyway for the 
reasons stated above.

    I've gotten the multiple data manipulations per form to work correctly.

broader functionality can make the demonstration much more functional and

place with each dynamic page access (and all securely too).
    I've examined the ForwardSQL page for the past 15 minutes and it hardly 
seems to be worthwhile to me.  The site says that they're built on Open 
Standards but that doesn't mean that their souce code is open or available.  
They are selling the package for $950.  It is a web-based MySQL 
administration package (similar to the one I was working on before) that 
provides an html frontend for table creation/modification/removal etc.  It 
does not create dynamic web pages from the data elements.  It enables you 
(or any user) to modify the database without writing MySQL code directly.  I 
didn't see a mention of transactions or rollbacks.  On the overview page, 
they suggest that you can store updates in a temporary table for review 
before they are committed but this can be done easily in any database.  
Maybe I missed something wonderful about it but ForwardSQL seems to just be 
a closed source front end to MySQL that we don't really need (since our 
tables are already almost complete, we have the hard code which defined 
them, and we have dynamic reads, updates, and deletes already working 
correctly).  Let me know if you have a different perspective.
    Tonight, I intend to test the multiple process handling thoroughly 
before I'm ready to leave it alone as done and stable for future usage.

June 25

I have read this carefully and I have mixed feelings about it.  Stable 
builds of opensource software end in an even sub-version number if they are 
reliable and an odd one if they are developmental/unstable/implementing beta 
features etc.  This means that Perl version 5.6 is a stable release that 
they want normal people to use as it has passed all the regression testing 
and meets all their stability requirements to be used widely.  Perl 5.7 on 
the other hand should only be used by Perl developers who are werking 
towards Perl 5.8 since it has not likely passed all the tests and is the 
ground to experiment with potential new implementations or features.  Perl 
5.7 might crash everytime you do something simple (depending on what 
developmental features were compiled into the particular build you got).  
The version of MySQL that we are currently using is the most recent stable 
version that I saw when I downloaded it (version 3.22.32).  Any MySQL driver 
that is in the under-development (3.23.xx) tree may not be stable or 
reliable.  Since we are in a development phase of 800Tele, I wouldn't worry 
too much if the database server crashed once in a while but if the 
BerkeleyDB component never makes it into a stable release build of MySQL 
(like the upcoming 3.24), I might be worried about employing a database 
suite that is known to not have been held to the same standards as release 
versions.  We may develop on 3.23.xx and find it to be perfectly stable and 
then it might not be a concern.  My recommendation is to stick with database 
engines that are most likely to be very stable.  With that in mind, would 
you like me to install this development version of MySQL (3.23.18) so that 
we can see how difficult it will be to enable our code to benefit from the 
transactional features mentioned by Mike?  TTFN & Shalom.

-Pip

This file was created by Pip Stuart on June 28th, 2000 for the purpose
of describing the software functionality developed thus far for
800Telephone.

The system is primarily composed of 3 programs:
    index.cgi - The default script which validates passwords and handles
                all secure administration processing.
    dp.cgi    - This script is a slimmed version of index.cgi which
                specializes in DynamicPages only.  It lets index.cgi
                validate the login and takes the handoff from there.
    pw.pl     - This is utility employed by the above scripts to
                handle an abstracted method for generating and
                processing unique session identification codes.

Almost everything in the system (from users to protected pages to data
fields to images) has 3 different permissions associated with it.  They
are: Read, Insert, and Delete.  The system validation checks each
permission level according to the requested operation.  Lower permission
numbers are more secure which means that a user with permissions
Read=0, Insert=0, & Delete=0 is completely unrestricted.  As permissions
ascend, the limitations on available options increase.  For now, a user
with Read=256, Insert=256, & Delete=256 is the most restricted user
named customer.  Priviledged users can specify the levels which limit
the use of each operation.  This means that an administrator (or
superuser with premissions 0,0,0) could grant full access to all users
or specify any number of arbitrary groups to partition users according
to permission levels and accessible options.  It will be meaningful for
the remainder of this document to describe all operations from the
perspective of a system administrator to detail each included function
and feature.  Every user with poorer permission levels will have
diminished access according to the administrator's designation.

For a user to be able to read a protected page (or view a particular
dynamic image), the user must have a Read permission level that is less
than or equal to the Read level associated with the page (or image).
For a user to be able to overwrite a protected page, the user must have
an Insert permission level and a Delete permission level that are both
less than or equal to the levels associated with the page.
For a user to be able to delete a protected page (or graphic file), the
user must have a Delete permission level less than or equal to that of
the page (or image).  Individual database element modifications have the
same properties.

Let's assume that there exists an account in the system for a user named
"superman" with a password of "souper" who has the highest permissions
(0,0,0).  Superman can point his browser to the login script (currently
http://24.16.72.254/demo/index.cgi) and specify "superman" and "souper"
as his Username and Password respectively in order to login to the
system.  If an incorrect password was supplied, an error message is
returned and the account name (in this case "superman") is written to a
logfile containing failed login attempts with timestamps.  If any user
supplies 3 errant passwords within a single hour, their account is
automatically locked for a 24 hour period.  Each account has an
associated hint field.  If a user has forgotten their password, they can
check the box trailing "Show hint?" and the Login will return with their
hint (this will not count as a failed login attempt either).

After "superman" has logged in, he will be presented with a field for
specifying search criteria to limit the protected pages to be listed.
The default value of "*" requests all files.  Currently, there are only
a handful of protected pages or images so it is not overwhelming to
request all files but as the system is used more widely, far too many
pages will be stored to show to superman everytime he examines the file
list.  If too many pages are found, superman's browser may crash since
the resulting page could scroll down for thousands of pages and overrun
his free system resources.  Therefore, it makes sense to specify pattern
matching criteria to determine which pages should be listed.  If a list
of only those files stored in the image directory was desired, superman
could replace "*" with "/img/*" to show every file that has a PageName
beginning with "/img/" (and is therefore stored in the server's image
directory).  Superman could specify multiple stars ("*") if he wanted a
more complex search.  Each star will match zero (0) or more characters
of any kind.

Having specified a search criteria of "*.htm*" to show a listing of all
available HTML files and clicking "List Protected Pages", superman is
shown a page containing a link at the top which goes back to the login
page and a welcome message relating the validation of the newly
allocated session code and the designated permission levels associated
with his account (in this case: Read=0, Insert=0, Delete=0).  Below
those is displayed a table containing options for each of the files
whose PageName matched his search criteria.  Each of these HTML pages
can be read, edited, or deleted.  Clicking the button to read any
particular page will render the page dynamically within a frame which
describes what the entire page would look like if it were being viewed
directly through dp.cgi.  The edit option will enable superman to modify
the PageName, permission levels, or contents of any file.  The delete
option removes the file (right now, this is permanent, but I'm
considering a trashcan scheme to make deletion less drastic).

Below the matched pages table is a small table which can be used to
create new files (for webpages or images or anything which can be stored
as a file).  A PageName can be specified and a new empty file will be
created or superman could select a local file (from his own computer) to
upload to the server as the initial contents of the new file.  This
operation will fail if the file already exists in the file system or the
database.  If it exists in the database, it must first be deleted by a
qualified user before a new file of the same name can be created.  If
the name is not in the database but is only found in the file system, an
administrator of the server will have to remove the file (for security
reasons) before it can be created.

The table following contains user administration options.  Superman
could use the fields in the first row to create a new user in the system
with initial values for their username, password, hint, permission
levels, and session time limit.  The next row can be used to update any
user accout.  New values can be provided to reset a user's forgotten
password, reassign their hint or permission levels, specify another time
limit, or lock/unlock the account.  The drop-down selection in the
Username field describes each username, permission levels, time limit,
and locked status (U or L) all separated by colons (:).  The last row
can be used to select a user to remove permanently from the system.

The following button labeled "Change Group Settings" goes to a page
which contains all of the defined group settings.  This page can be used
to create, modify, or delete group definitions.  When users login, each
group is checked in order (top-down).  The first group that contains a
range which the user's permission levels fit into is the group that the
user is affiliated with (even if later groups also match).  If a
DefaultPage is specified for a user group, the protected page with the
same PageName is displayed with dp.cgi after a login instead of the file
list and administration options.  Any number of groups can be created
(limited by disk space) each with their own respective DefaultPage to
which matching users will be ushered.  The check boxes apply to users
who match groups that don't have DefaultPages (because they have enough
access to see the file list and other administrative features).  Each
box limits which components are displayed to logged in members of that
group.

The button below that labeled "Change Your Settings" goes to a screen
for updating personal account settings.  This can be used to change your
password, hint, time limit, or search string.  For superman to change
his password, he'll have to supply his old one and then repeat the new
one correctly (and it must be at least 4 characters) for the update to
succeed.

The last button is simply to "Logout".

The above describes the administrative features of the 800Telephone
system (as of June 28th).  Below, I will describe the methods which can
be used to embed database requests within html pages in order to produce
secure dynamic pages.  The system also has the ability to process
embedded database insertions and updates from dynamic pages.  These
contents can be added to html files though the page edit option from the
administrative list or directly on a workstation before being uploaded
when a new PageName is created.

There are currently two different ways to specify a database field to be
dynamically inserted into html each time the page is accessed.  The
first method is just a minimized cryptic code for describing any field
while the second is just a more verbose method.  Functionally, the two
are equivalent.  In html, the first would look like:
    <h3>Some Field is: {id=1~Customer_Record.Type}</h3>
where "id" is the name of the primary field and "1" is the primary value
of the known record containing the desired field.  "Customer_Record" is
the name of the table that contains the field names "id" and "Type".
"Type" is the desired field that gets replaced into the html (if
permissions allow).  An equivalent html line to the above with the
second syntax method is:
    <h3>Some Field is: 
{PrimaryField{id}=PrimaryValue{1}~Database{demobase}.Table{Customer_Record}.DesiredField{Type}}</h3>
This second method must have each value enclosed in braces {} after the
field name.  The field names are: PrimaryField, PrimaryValue, Database,
Table, and DesiredField.  The Database field can be omitted for any
normal query since the default value is the main 800Telephone database
already (just as it was absent from the first example above but could be
provided there also as another value preceeding the table name separated
by a period).

There are several operations which can be embedded within dynamic pages
to update, modify, or delete data elements or records as well.  Any
number of these operations can be performed with a single submission.
Examples for each follow.

There may be several issues missing from the above description however,
it is my hope that an html/graphics designer could take this file, along
with a description of relevant database names and fields and a
description of what inputs and outputs are necessary or desired for each
particular page; I imagine that these three would be sufficient to fully
develop nearly all of the pages necessary for 800Telephone.

The method for updating data is relatively complex but it is a necessity
of the inherent power involved in performing multiple secure database
updates with each web form submission.  The main processes available are
insertions, updates, and deletions.  To insert, the logged in user must
have sufficient insert permissions.  Sufficient delete permissions are
required for deletes.  The user must have both delete and insert
permissions beyond the specified level for the data elements being
modified to perform an updating operation.  Any number of operations can
be performed within a single form submission and each one is validated
on an individual basis.

Each suboperation is encoded with operation numbers in each name field.
Listed here is an example of a simple insertion:
    <form action="dp.cgi" method="post">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich0bas" value="demobase">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich0tbl" value="Customer_Record">
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld0" value="Type"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut0val0" value=""><br>
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld1" value="Reason"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut0val1" value=""><br>
    <input type="hidden" name="wut0todo" value="insereco">
    <input type="hidden" name="pagename" value="customer0.htm">
    <input type="submit" name="submit" value="Create New Record"></form>
The (currently) available values for the hidden field "wut$Xtodo" (where
$X = the operation number, 0 in this case) are "insereco", "updtfiel",
and "delereco".  Operation numbers begin at 0 (zero) and proceed
sequentially (in decimal notation) upwards unbounded.  One submission
button could perform any number of inserts, updates, and deletes as long
as each is encoded sequentially according to the operation number.  To
perform any insert, the following fields are required:

  * "pagename" is a required field for every submitted form to tell
        which dynamic page to load after the submission is processed.
        (NOTE: When only pagename is specified, it's just like a normal
           link to the new dynamic page without any database changes.)
  * "wich$Xbas" must contain the name of the database into which data
        will be inserted.
  * "wich$Xtbl" is the table to receive the inserted data.
  * "wut$Xtodo" must contain "insereco" for an insertion.
  * "wut$Xfld$Y" is the name of the field you wish to provide an initial
        value for where the integer $Y ascends from 0 to the number of
        fields you wish to insert into the new record.
  * "wut$Xval$Y" is the corresponding value to insert into the specified
        database and table and field.  (NOTE: Any number of field and
        value pairs can be specified up to the total number of fields
        specified within the table.  Each value will be given a default
        if no entry for the field is designated.)

To perform an update, the following fields are required:

  * "pagename" to specify which page to load after the update is
        performed.
  * "wich$Xbas" must contain the name of the database from which data
        will be updated.
  * "wich$Xtbl" is the table to receive the data update.
  * "wut$Xtodo" must contain "updtfiel" for an update.
  * "nown$Xfld" is the name of the field (most likely the name of the
        primary key) which identifies the record you wish to update.
  * "nown$Xval" is the value of the field which is a unique
        identification value for the record you wish to update.
  * "wut$Xfld$Y" is the name of the field you wish to provide a new
        value for where the integer $Y ascends from 0 to the number of
        fields you wish to insert into the new record.
  * "wut$Xval$Y" is the corresponding value to update in the specified
        database and table and field.  (NOTE: Any number of field and
        value pairs can be specified up to the total number of fields
        specified within the table.  Each value will be retain it's
        original value if no entry for the field is specified.)

To perform a delete, the following fields are required:

  * "pagename" to specify which page to load after the update is
        performed.
  * "wich$Xbas" must contain the name of the database from which the
        data record will be removed.
  * "wich$Xtbl" is the table to delete the data from.
  * "wut$Xtodo" must contain "delereco" for an update.
  * "nown$Xfld" is the name of the field (most likely the name of the
        primary key) which identifies the record you wish to delete.
  * "nown$Xval" is the value of the field which is a unique
        identification value for the record you wish to delete.

Following is an exceptionally simple example of an insert, update and
delete all in a single form:
    <form action="dp.cgi" method="post">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich0bas" value="demobase">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich0tbl" value="Customer_Record">
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld0" value="Type"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut0val0" value=""><br>
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld1" 
value="RelationshipXq"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut0val1" value=""><br>
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch0fld2" value="Reason"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut0val2" value=""><br>
    <input type="hidden" name="wut0todo" value="insereco">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich1bas" value="demobase">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich1tbl" value="Customer_Record">
    Known Field?: <input type="text" name="nown1fld" value="id"><br>
    Known Value?: <input type="text" name="nown1val" value="3"><br>
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch1fld0" value="Type"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut1val0" value=""><br>
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch1fld1" 
value="RelationshipXq"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut1val1" value=""><br>
    Which Field?: <input type="text" name="wch1fld2" value="Reason"><br>
    What Value?:  <input type="text" name="wut1val2" value=""><br>
    <input type="hidden" name="wut1todo" value="updtfiel">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich2bas" value="demobase">
    <input type="hidden" name="wich2tbl" value="Customer_Record">
    Known Primary Field?: <input type="text" name="nown2fld" value="id"><br>
    Which Unique Value?:  <input type="text" name="nown2val" value="5"><br>
    <input type="hidden" name="wut2todo" value="delereco">
    <input type="hidden" name="pagename" value="customer0.htm">
    <input type="submit" name="submit" value="Return to Primary Customer 
Page With A Record Creation, Update, & Delete all at once!">
    </form>

Hopefully the above description is clear enough to describe the method
of my madness... I mean my genius =)  If you have questions, feel free
to pay me to answer them.  The remaining operation is a way to perform
selections (searches) on the database in order to arrange comparisons
and statistical evaluations generated from large portions of data.  I
will update this description once selections are operational and can be
described.  TTFN.

-Pip

July 6

I've been pouring over the code and ... well here is my analysis:
  I could change the submission structure to handle each field update on a 
single line.  The deletion of a record could also be distilled to a single 
line.  Inserting a new record would not be as easy to handle on a single 
line as the other two.  Insertions would probably have to remain similar to 
the current structure.
  To make these changes, I would have to throw out a lot of code and rewrite 
it since fundamental assumptions of the updating structure permeate both the 
entire password module and the dynamic pages script.
  I could probably finish rewriting and testing the modules by next Monday 
or Tuesday if it were necessary to do so.

  The system works as it is now (even if it is slightly more complex than it 
could have been).
  Redesigning and rewriting such fundamental components introduces 
significant opportunity for things to break  that are already working 
correctly.
  I don't think it's worth the time to rewrite so much Perl code just for 
the perceived benefit of more compacted (and more redundant) single-lined 
html code.

That's what I've found.  Hopefully we can discuss what more to do tomorrow 
afternoon.  TTFN.

-Pip
